## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Task: Kubernetes API Server Architecture and Extension Guide

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--8c9c67c0 (mirror of kubernetes/kubernetes) (stripped snapshot)
**Output:** Write your document to `/workspace/documentation.md`

## Objective

Produce a subsystem architecture and extension guide for the apiserver library with request-path flow and extension tradeoffs.

## Scope

Focus on the Kubernetes apiserver library subsystem.
Your document must explain component responsibilities, end-to-end flow, and extension or operational tradeoffs.

## Content Expectations

Address all of the following in your own structure:
- subsystem purpose, boundaries, and upstream/downstream dependencies
- key components and how responsibilities are split
- end-to-end control/request flow with concrete repository evidence
- failure modes, limits, and design tradeoffs
- extension points, customization hooks, and associated risks
- a concise map of the most important files/directories used in your analysis

## Quality Bar

- Cite concrete file paths from the repository.
- Explain behavior and interactions, not just API signatures.
- Include at least one section on operational implications (performance, reliability, or maintainability).
- Do not fabricate classes, functions, or files.

## Anti-Requirements

- Do not output `doc.go`.
- Do not provide shallow bullet dumps without system flow explanation.
- Do not rely on external docs not present in the workspace.

482026-03-11T07:07:11.945248agentmessage-
I am thinking...: I now have a comprehensive understanding of the Kubernetes apiserver library. Let me organize my findings to write the documentation:

1. **Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries**: The `k8s.io/apiserver` library (at `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/`) is the generic API server framework that powers all Kubernetes API servers. It provides the infrastructure for serving REST APIs, authentication, authorization, admission control, storage, and more.

2. **Key Components**:
   - `pkg/server/` - Core server infrastructure (GenericAPIServer, Config, handler chain)
   - `pkg/endpoints/` - HTTP endpoint installation (APIInstaller, handlers for CRUD operations)
   - `pkg/admission/` - Admission control framework (interfaces, chain, plugins)
   - `pkg/authentication/` - Authentication subsystem
   - `pkg/authorization/` - Authorization subsystem
   - `pkg/registry/` - REST storage abstractions (Store, strategies)
   - `pkg/storage/` - Storage layer (etcd3, cacher)
   - `pkg/server/options/` - Configuration options (RecommendedOptions)

3. **Server Chain**: Three-server delegation chain:
   - Aggregator Server (kube-aggregator) → Kube API Server (core) → API Extensions Server (CRDs)
   - Implemented via `DelegationTarget` interface in `genericapiserver.go`

4. **Handler Chain** (from `config.go`):
   - `BuildHandlerChainFunc` wraps the API handler
   - Default: `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` in `config.go`
   - Stages: Authentication → Authorization → Priority/Fairness → Admission → REST endpoint

5. **Request Flow** (from `create.go`):
   - HTTP request → APIServerHandler.FullHandlerChain → Director → GoRestfulContainer/NonGoRestfulMux
   - createHandler: read body → decode → validate → admission → store

6. **Storage Layer**:
   - `storage.Interface` - abstract storage int

---

## What the Document Covers

### 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies
Explains that `k8s.io/apiserver` (at `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/`) is a reusable library — not a binary — that provides the complete infrastructure for serving Kubernetes REST APIs. It draws clear boundaries between what this library owns versus `k8s.io/apimachinery`, `k8s.io/apiextensions-apiserver`, and `k8s.io/kube-aggregator`, and maps the upstream/downstream dependency graph.

### 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split
Seven major subsystems are analyzed with concrete file citations:
- **`pkg/server/`** — `Config`, `GenericAPIServer`, `DelegationTarget`, `APIServerHandler`, lifecycle hooks, and shutdown signals
- **`pkg/endpoints/`** — `APIInstaller` route registration and per-verb handlers (`create.go`, `patch.go`, `watch.go`)
- **`pkg/admission/`** — `MutationInterface`/`ValidationInterface`, `chainAdmissionHandler`, re-invocation policy, and built-in plugins
- **`pkg/registry/`** — `rest.Storage` interface hierarchy and the generic `Store` with its strategy pattern
- **`pkg/storage/`** — `storage.Interface`, etcd3 implementation, and the watch `Cacher`
- **`pkg/server/options/`** — `RecommendedOptions` as the canonical extension server configuration entry point

### 3. End-to-End Request Flow
Three concrete flows are traced with line-level evidence:
- **Server chain routing** — how `DelegationTarget.UnprotectedHandler()` chains Aggregator → Core → API Extensions
- **Handler chain** — the 11-stage filter pipeline from panic recovery through APF to the Director
- **CREATE handler** — the complete lifecycle from body read

This system is also pluggable and composed of multiple authorizers\\\\n106:     (e.g., RBAC, Node, Webhook). A single\\\\n136: `Scheme` object is created for each API group and is responsible for the following key\\\\n137: capabilities:\\\\n138: \\\\n139: *   **Type Registration and Mapping:** The `Scheme`'s primary role is to map a GroupVersionKind\\\\n140:     (GVK) to its corresponding Go type and back. This process also relies on the `deepcopy-gen`\\\\n141:     tool to create `DeepCopy()` methods for each type, which is critical for ensuring that\\\\n142:     objects returned from caches are never modified directly.\\\\n143: \\\\n144: *   **API Conversion:** The `Scheme` stores the conversion functions that translate objects\\\\n145:     between different API versions. Watch Cache\\\\n198: \\\\n199: To handle the high volume of watch requests from controllers without overwhelming etcd, the\\\\n200: apiserver uses a **watch cache**. The implementation can be found in\\\\n201: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/`.\\\\n202: \\\\n203: *   **Initialization:** The cacher first performs a `LIST` to get the current state of all\\\\n204:     objects and a `ResourceVersion` for that point-in-time. It then starts a `WATCH` from\\\\n205:     that version to ensure a consistent stream of events.\\\\n206: *   **Serving from Cache:** Most list and watch requests are served from this in-memory cache, which\\\\n207:     dramatically reduces the load on etcd. Consistent reads are also served from the\\\\n208:     cache. This is achieved by first fetching the revision number of the latest write from\\\\n209:     etcd. The server then ensures the cache is at least that recent\\u2014waiting for it to\\\\n210:     refresh if necessary\\u2014before serving the request.\\\\n211: *   **Fallback to Storage:** If a client request cannot be served from the\\\\n212:     cache's buffer, the request \\\\\\\"falls through\\\\\\\" to the underlying etcd storage.\\\\n213: *   **Bookmarks:** The cacher uses bookmark events to track the latest `ResourceVersion` for\\\\n214:     unchanged objects. This prevents the cache's `ResourceVersion` from becoming too old,\\\\n215:     which avoids the need for expensive relist operations from etcd when the objects have\\\\n216:     not been modified.\\\\n217: \\\\n218: ## 5. Conflict Resolution\\\\n219: \\\\n220: *   **Optimistic Concurrency via `resourceVersion`:** Clients are expected to perform updates using a\\\\n221:     read-modify-write workflow. The apiserver uses the `resourceVersion` field of every\\\\n222:     object to enforce optimistic concurrency. This `resourceVersion` is not an arbitrary number;\\\\n223:     it maps directly to etcd's globally consistent `mod_revision`. When a client submits an\\\\n224:     update (`PUT` or `PATCH`), it must provide the `resourceVersion` of the object it based its\\\\n225:     modifications on. If the `resourceVersion` on the server does not match the current\\\\n226:     `mod_revision` in etcd, the server rejects the request with a `409 Conflict` error. This\\\\n227:     forces the client to re-read the object, resolve the conflict, and resubmit with the new\\\\n228:     `resourceVersion`.\\\\n229: *   **Server-Side Apply:** A declarative, \\\\\\\"intent-based\\\\\\\" patch. The server maintains a\\\\n230:     `managedFields` section in the object's metadata to track which \\\\\\\"manager\\\\\\\" (e.g., a\\\\n231:     controller) owns each field. This allows multiple actors to manage different parts of the\\\\n232:     same object without overwriting each other's changes.\\\\n233: \\\\n234: ## 6. The audit\\\\n249:     policy controls what is logged and at which stage of a request.\\\\n250: *   **Security:**\\\\n251:     *   **mTLS:** The primary authentication mechanism for system components.\\\\n252:     *   **Service Account Token Issuance:** The `kube-apiserver` acts as an OIDC provider,\\\\n253:         issuing and validating JWTs for `ServiceAccount`s.\\\\n254: \\\\n255: ## 8. The construction of this delegation chain can be found in the `CreateServerChain`\\n13: function in `cmd/kube-apiserver/app/server.go`.\\n14: \\n15: ```mermaid\\n16: graph TD\\n17:     subgraph Incoming Request\\n18:         direction LR\\n19:         A[User/Client] --> B{/apis/apps/v1/deployments};\\n20:     end\\n21: \\n22:     subgraph kube-apiserver process\\n23:         direction LR\\n24:         B --> C[Aggregator Server];\\n25:         C -- Not an APIService --> D[Kube API Server];\\n26:         D -- Handles Request --> E[REST Storage];\\n27:         C -- Is an APIService --> F[Proxy to Extension API Server];\\n28:         D -- Not a Core API --> G[API Extensions Server];\\n29:         G -- Handles CRD --> E;\\n30:     end\\n31: ```\\n32: \\n33: 1.  **Aggregator Server (`kube-aggregator`):**\\n34:     *   **Purpose:** Handles the `apiregistration.k8s.io` API and acts as a reverse proxy for\\n35:         extension API servers. This functionality was designed to allow third-party APIs to be\\n36:         \\\"aggregated\\\" into the main Kubernetes API server seamlessly.\\n37:     *   **Mechanism:** It watches `APIService` objects. When a request arrives (e.g., for\\n38:         `/apis/mycompany.com/v1/myresources`), it checks if an `APIService` has \\\"claimed\\\"\\n39:         that path. If so, it uses a `ServiceResolver` to find the IP of the backing\\n40:         `Service` and proxies the request.\\n41:     *   **Use Case:** This pattern is for programmatic, high-control extensions that require\\n42:         custom business logic (e.g., non-CRUD subresources like `/logs`) or alternative\\n43:         storage backends.\\n44:     *   **Delegation:** If no `APIService` matches, it delegates the request to the next\\n45:         server in the chain.\\n46: \\n47: 2.  **Kube API Server (Core):**\\n48:     *   **Purpose:** Serves all the built-in Kubernetes APIs (`core/v1`, `apps/v1`, etc.).\\n49:     *   **Mechanism:** This is the main server, configured with all the core REST storage\\n50:         strategies.\\n51:     *   **Delegation:** If a request is for a path that is not a core API (e.g., for a CRD),\\n52:         it delegates the request to the next server in the chain.\\n53: \\n54: 3.  **API Extensions Server (`apiextensions-apiserver`):**\\n55:     *   **Purpose:** Handles the `apiextensions.k8s.io` API, which manages\\n56:         `CustomResourceDefinition` objects (CRDs). The evolution of CRDs from a simple extension\\n57:         mechanism to a feature-rich system with validation, versioning, and defaulting is\\n58:         documented in a series of KEPs, starting with the graduation to GA in Kubernetes v1.16.\\n59:     *   **Mechanism:** When a CRD is created, this server dynamically creates and installs a\\n60:         new REST storage handler for the new resource, making it immediately available.\\n61:     *   **Use Case:** CRDs are the most common extension pattern, offering a declarative,\\n62:         schema-based way to define new resource types that are stored in etcd and require no\\n63:         custom API server code.\\n64:     *   **Delegation:** It is the end of the chain. If it cannot handle a request, a `404 Not\\n65:         Found` is returned.\\n66: \\n67: ## 2. Handler Chain\\n68: \\n69: Every request flows through a standard chain of HTTP handlers (filters). The request body\\n70: is not deserialized until it has passed authentication and authorization. The default handler\\n71: chain is constructed by the `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` function in\\n72: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go`.\\n73: \\n74: ```mermaid\\n75: sequenceDiagram\\n76:     participant Client\\n77:     participant Handler Chain\\n78:     participant Authentication\\n79:     participant Authorization\\n80:     participant Priority and Fairness\\n81:     participant Admission Control\\n82:     participant REST Endpoint\\n83: \\n84:     Client->>Handler Chain: Request\\n85:     Handler Chain->>Authentication: Authenticate\\n86:     Authentication-->>Handler Chain: User Info\\n87:     Handler Chain->>Authorization: Authorize\\n88:     Authorization-->>Handler Chain: Allowed/Denied\\n89:     Handler Chain->>Priority and Fairness: Classify & Queue\\n90:     Priority and Fairness-->>Handler Chain: Proceed\\n91:     Handler Chain->>Admission Control: Mutate & Validate\\n92:     Admission Control-->>Handler Chain: Object OK\\n93:     Handler Chain->>REST Endpoint: Handle\\n94:     REST Endpoint-->>Handler Chain: Response\\n95:     Handler Chain-->>Client: Response\\n96: ```\\n97: \\n98: The handler chain consists of the following stages:\\n99: \\n100: 1.  **Authentication (`pkg/authentication`):** This filter identifies the user. The system is\\n101:     pluggable and composed of multiple authenticators (e.g., client certs, bearer tokens, OIDC).\\n102:     The identity of the user is determined by the first authenticator in the chain that successfully\\n103:     identifies the user.\\n104: 2.  **Authorization (`pkg/authorization`):** This filter checks if the user is permitted to\\n105:     perform the action. This system is also pluggable and composed of multiple authorizers\\n106:     (e.g., RBAC, Node, Webhook). Each authorizer may respond with either allow, deny, or no opinion.\\n107:     If the response is no opinion, the request is passed to the next authorizer in the chain.\\n108: 3.  **Priority and Fairness (`pkg/util/flowcontrol`):** This subsystem manages request\\n109:     concurrency, classifying requests into `FlowSchema`s and `PriorityLevel`s to prevent\\n110:     overload. This feature was introduced to prevent high traffic from overwhelming the API\\n111:     server and to ensure that critical cluster operations are not starved.\\n112: 4.  **Admission Control (`pkg/admission`):** This is the primary mechanism for policy\\n113:     enforcement. It is only at this stage that the request body is deserialized into an\\n114:     object. It is a chain of plugins that can mutate or validate an object. The built-in Pod\\n115:     Security admission controller is a key example of this, enforcing Pod Security Standards\\n116:     at the namespace level.\\n117: 5.  **REST Endpoint Handling (`pkg/endpoints`):** The request is finally dispatched to the\\n118:     appropriate REST handler, which is installed by the `APIInstaller`.\\n119: \\n120: ## 3. API Group Registration\\n121: \\n122: The high-level steps for introducing an API are:\\n123: \\n124: 1.  **Define Types:** Create or modify the Go structs in the `types.go` file for the API group.\\n125: 2.  **Generate Code:** Use the code generators provided by the Kubernetes project to create the required\\n126:     boilerplate methods for deep-copy, conversion, and defaulting.\\n127: 3.  **Implement the `Strategy`:** Write the custom business logic and validation for the\\n128:     resource in its `Strategy` object.\\n129: 4.  **Register and Install:** Create the `APIGroupInfo` struct, bundling the `Scheme` and the\\n130:     `Strategy`-configured storage, and pass it to the `GenericAPIServer`'s `InstallAPIGroup`\\n131:     method.\\n132: \\n133: ### The API Group Registry\\n134: \\n135: The `runtime.Scheme` acts as a central registry for an API group's type information. A single\\n136: `Scheme` object is created for each API group and is responsible for the following key\\n137: capabilities:\\n138: \\n139: *   **Type Registration and Mapping:** The `Scheme`'s primary role is to map a GroupVersionKind\\n140:     (GVK) to its corresponding Go type and back. This process also relies on the `deepcopy-gen`\\n141:     tool to create `DeepCopy()` methods for each type, which is critical for ensuring that\\n142:     objects returned from caches are never modified directly.\\n143: \\n144: *   **API Conversion:** The `Scheme` stores the conversion functions that translate objects\\n145:     between different API versions. These functions are typically generated by the\\n146:     `conversion-gen` tool and enable the **hub-and-spoke** model.\\n147: \\n148: *   **Defaulting:** The `Scheme` registers defaulting functions that populate optional fields in\\n149:     an object. These are usually generated by the `defaulter-gen` tool.\\n150: \\n151: *   **Declarative Validation:** The `Scheme` can store and execute code-generated validation\\n152:     functions, providing a baseline level of validation. This is distinct from the primary,\\n153:     handwritten business logic validation, which is handled by the `Strategy` object.\\n154: \\n155: ### The `APIGroupInfo` Struct and `Strategy` Object\\n156: \\n157: With a populated `Scheme`, the API group is registered with the `GenericAPIServer` by bundling\\n158: the `Scheme` with the storage backend and versioning information into an `APIGroupInfo` struct.\\n159: \\n160: ```mermaid\\n161: graph TD\\n162:     subgraph Server Configuration\\n163:         A[APIGroupInfo for apps v1];\\n164:         A --> B{Scheme: Knows Deployment v1};\\n165:         A --> C{Storage: deployments RESTStorage};\\n166:         A --> D{Version Priority: v1, v1beta1};\\n167:     end\\n168: \\n169:     subgraph RESTStorage Implementation\\n170:         C --> E[genericregistry.Store];\\n171:         E --> F[etcd client];\\n172:         E --> G[Deployment Strategy];\\n173:     end\\n174: \\n175:     subgraph Server Runtime\\n176:         H[GenericAPIServer] -- InstallAPIGroup --> I[APIInstaller];\\n177:         I -- Uses --> A;\\n178:         I --> J{Register /apis/apps/v1/deployments};\\n179:         J --> K[HTTP Handler];\\n180:         K -- On Request --> C;\\n181:     end\\n182: ```\\n183: \\n184: The registration process follows these steps:\\n185: \\n186: 1.  **`APIGroupInfo` Construction:** For each API group, an `APIGroupInfo` struct is created,\\n187:     which contains the populated `Scheme`, a map of resources to their storage\\n188:     implementations, and an ordered list of **Version Priority**.\\n189: \\n190: 2.  **REST Storage Instantiation:** For each resource, a `genericregistry.Store` is created. It\\n191:     is configured with a resource-specific `Strategy` object that contains the core business\\n192:     logic (e.g., handwritten validation).\\n193: \\n194: 3.  **API Group Installation:** The `GenericAPIServer`'s `InstallAPIGroup` method takes the\\n195:     `APIGroupInfo` and uses an `APIInstaller` to expose the resources as HTTP endpoints.\\n196: \\n197: ## 4. Watch Cache\\n198: \\n199: To handle the high volume of watch requests from controllers without overwhelming etcd, the\\n200: apiserver uses a **watch cache**. The implementation can be found in\\n201: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/`.\\n202: \\n203: *   **Initialization:** The cacher first performs a `LIST` to get the current state of all\\n204:     objects and a `ResourceVersion` for that point-in-time. It then starts a `WATCH` from\\n205:     that version to ensure a consistent stream of events.\\n206: *   **Serving from Cache:** Most list and watch requests are served from this in-memory cache, which\\n207:     dramatically reduces the load on etcd. Consistent reads are also served from the\\n208:     cache. This is achieved by first fetching the revision number of the latest write from\\n209:     etcd. The server then ensures the cache is at least that recent\\u2014waiting for it to\\n210:     refresh if necessary\\u2014before serving the request.\\n211: *   **Fallback to Storage:** If a client request cannot be served from the\\n212:     cache's buffer, the request \\\"falls through\\\" to the underlying etcd storage.\\n213: *   **Bookmarks:** The cacher uses bookmark events to track the latest `ResourceVersion` for\\n214:     unchanged objects. This prevents the cache's `ResourceVersion` from becoming too old,\\n215:     which avoids the need for expensive relist operations from etcd when the objects have\\n216:     not been modified.\\n217: \\n218: ## 5. Conflict Resolution\\n219: \\n220: *   **Optimistic Concurrency via `resourceVersion`:** Clients are expected to perform updates using a\\n221:     read-modify-write workflow. The apiserver uses the `resourceVersion` field of every\\n222:     object to enforce optimistic concurrency. This `resourceVersion` is not an arbitrary number;\\n223:     it maps directly to etcd's globally consistent `mod_revision`. When a client submits an\\n224:     update (`PUT` or `PATCH`), it must provide the `resourceVersion` of the object it based its\\n225:     modifications on. If the `resourceVersion` on the server does not match the current\\n226:     `mod_revision` in etcd, the server rejects the request with a `409 Conflict` error. This\\n227:     forces the client to re-read the object, resolve the conflict, and resubmit with the new\\n228:     `resourceVersion`.\\n229: *   **Server-Side Apply:** A declarative, \\\"intent-based\\\" patch. The server maintains a\\n230:     `managedFields` section in the object's metadata to track which \\\"manager\\\" (e.g., a\\n231:     controller) owns each field. This allows multiple actors to manage different parts of the\\n232:     same object without overwriting each other's changes.\\n233: \\n234: ## 6. Discovery and OpenAPI\\n235: \\n236: Apiservers serve the `/apis` discovery endpoints and the `/openapi/v2` and `/openapi/v3`\\n237: specifications. The generation of the OpenAPI specification is a multi-stage process.\\n238: \\n239: *   **`openapi-gen`**: This tool reflects on Go structs, reads godoc comments, and looks at\\n240:     validation struct tags to generate a map of all API definitions.\\n241: *   **`zz_generated.openapi.go`**: The output is a large Go file containing a\\n242:     `GetOpenAPIDefinitions` function.\\n243: *   **Runtime**: The `GenericAPIServer` calls this generated function to build the final OpenAPI\\n244:     JSON spec that it serves to clients.\\n245: \\n246: ## 7. Security & Observability\\n247: \\n248: *   **Audit (`pkg/audit`):** The apiserver has a policy-driven event logging pipeline. The audit\\n249:     policy controls what is logged and at which stage of a request.\\n250: *   **Security:**\\n251:     *   **mTLS:** The primary authentication mechanism for system components.\\n252:     *   **Service Account Token Issuance:** The `kube-apiserver` acts as an OIDC provider,\\n253:         issuing and validating JWTs for `ServiceAccount`s.\\n254: \\n255: ## 8. Streaming Protocols\\n256: \\n257: *   **Websockets:** The apiserver uses websockets to upgrade HTTP\\n258:     connections for interactive, streaming protocols like `exec`, `attach`, and\\n259:     `port-forward`. The `UpgradeAwareProxyHandler` manages this process.\\n260: \", \"url\": \"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--8c9c67c0@8c9c67c000104450cfc5a5f48053a9a84b73cf93/-/blob/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/ARCHITECTURE.md\"}, \"isError\": false}"

Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n### Purpose\n\nThe `k8s.io/apiserver` library (located at `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/`) is the **generic API server framework** that underpins every Kubernetes API server process. It is not a standalone binary; it is a reusable library that provides the complete infrastructure for serving REST APIs over HTTPS, including authentication, authorization, admission control, serialization, storage abstraction, watch caching, and graceful lifecycle management.\n\nThe library's central abstraction is `GenericAPIServer` (`pkg/server/genericapiserver.go`), a composable server instance that can be configured with different API groups, handler chains, and storage backends. The `kube-apiserver` binary itself is built by composing three `GenericAPIServer` instances into a delegation chain.\n\n### Boundaries\n\n**In scope** (what this library owns):\n- HTTP serving infrastructure (TLS, mux routing, handler chain construction)\n- Authentication and authorization framework interfaces and union implementations\n- Admission control plugin framework and built-in plugins (webhook, CEL, namespace, resource quota)\n- REST endpoint installation (`APIInstaller`) and CRUD handler dispatch\n- Generic registry (`Store`) and storage abstraction (`storage.Interface`)\n- Watch cache (`storage/cacher/`) that sits between the registry and etcd\n- API group registration (`APIGroupInfo`, `InstallAPIGroup`)\n- Server lifecycle management (startup hooks, graceful shutdown signals)\n- OpenAPI/discovery endpoint generation\n\n**Out of scope** (owned by other libraries):\n- Type definitions for built-in resources \u2192 `k8s.io/api`\n- Scheme, serialization, and conversion primitives \u2192 `k8s.io/apimachinery`\n- CRD-specific handling \u2192 `k8s.io/apiextensions-apiserver`\n- Aggregation layer proxy \u2192 `k8s.io/kube-aggregator`\n- Client libraries \u2192 `k8s.io/client-go`\n\n### Upstream/Downstream Dependencies\n\n```\nk8s.io/apimachinery          \u2190 runtime.Scheme, GVK, serialization, watch\nk8s.io/api backend\n\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\n              k8s.io/apiserver  (this GenericAPIServer\n```\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### 2.1 `pkg/server/` \u2014 Server Core\n\n**`config.go`** defines the two primary configuration types:\n\n- `Config` \u2014 the complete configuration struct for a `GenericAPIServer`. Its fields cover TLS serving (`SecureServing`), authentication (`Authentication`), authorization (`Authorization`), admission (`AdmissionControl`), flow control (`FlowControl`), audit (`AuditBackend`, `AuditPolicyRuleEvaluator`), storage (`RESTOptionsGetter`, `ResourceTransformers`), and lifecycle tuning (`ShutdownDelayDuration`, `MaxRequestsInFlight`, `MaxMutatingRequestsInFlight`). The comment in the source explicitly groups fields by importance for composers.\n\n- `RecommendedConfig` \u2014 embeds `Config` and adds `SharedInformerFactory` and `ClientConfig`, providing the standard starting point for extension API servers.\n\nThe `Config.Complete()` method (line 702) seals the configuration into a `CompletedConfig`, filling in derived fields (external address, OpenAPI version, discovery addresses, request info resolver). Only a `CompletedConfig` can call `New()` to produce a `GenericAPIServer`.\n\n**`genericapiserver.go`** defines `GenericAPIServer` and the `DelegationTarget` interface:\n\n```go\n// DelegationTarget is an interface which allows for composition of API servers\ntype DelegationTarget interface {\n    UnprotectedHandler() http.Handler\n    PostStartHooks() map[string]postStartHookEntry\n    PreShutdownHooks() map[string]preShutdownHookEntry\n    HealthzChecks() []healthz.HealthChecker\n    NextDelegate() DelegationTarget\n    PrepareRun() preparedGenericAPIServer\n    MuxAndDiscoveryCompleteSignals() map[string]<-chan struct{}\n    Destroy()\n}\n```\n\nThis interface is what makes the three-server delegation chain possible. Each server in the chain holds a reference to the next via `delegationTarget DelegationTarget` (line 220). When a request arrives for a path that the current server does not handle, it falls through to `delegationTarget.UnprotectedHandler()`.\n\n**`handler.go`** defines `APIServerHandler`, the HTTP routing core:\n\n```go\ntype APIServerHandler struct {\n    FullHandlerChain   http.Handler        // filter chain wrapping Director\n    GoRestfulContainer *restful.Container  // go-restful for /api and /apis paths\n    NonGoRestfulMux    *mux.PathRecorderMux // fallback for health, metrics, etc.\n    Director           http.Handler        // routes between the two\n}\n```\n\nThe `Director.ServeHTTP` method (line 121) inspects the request path against registered go-restful `WebService` root paths. If a match is found, it dispatches to `GoRestfulContainer`; otherwise it falls through to `NonGoRestfulMux`. This dual-mux design exists because go-restful is needed for OpenAPI generation but is too strict for delegation fallthrough.\n\n**`hooks.go`** implements `PostStartHookFunc` and `PreShutdownHookFunc`. Each `PostStartHook` is run in its own goroutine after the server starts listening. Critically, each hook is automatically wired to a `/readyz` health check (`postStartHookHealthz`) that returns failure until the hook's `done` channel is closed (line 109). This means the server will not report ready until all post-start hooks complete.\n\n**`lifecycle_signals.go`** defines the named channel-based signals that coordinate the shutdown sequence: `ShutdownInitiated`, `AfterShutdownDelayDuration`, `NotAcceptingNewRequest`, `InFlightRequestsDrained`, `HTTPServerStoppedListening`, `PreShutdownHooksStopped`, and `MuxAndDiscoveryComplete`.\n\n### 2.2 `pkg/endpoints/` \u2014 HTTP Endpoint Installation\n\n**`installer.go`** defines `APIInstaller`, which takes an `APIGroupVersion` (containing a map of resource names to `rest.Storage` implementations) and registers HTTP routes in the `GoRestfulContainer`. For each resource, it introspects which `rest` interfaces the storage implements (e.g., `rest.Getter`, `rest.Creater`, `rest.Updater`, `rest.Watcher`) and registers the corresponding HTTP verbs. The `action` struct (line 69) captures the verb, path, and parameters for each registered route.\n\n**`handlers/`** contains the per-verb HTTP handler functions:\n- `create.go` \u2014 `createHandler`: reads body, decodes, runs field manager, calls admission, calls `r.Create()`\n- `get.go` \u2014 handles GET (single object and list)\n- `update.go` \u2014 handles PUT\n- `patch.go` \u2014 handles PATCH (JSON merge, strategic merge, server-side apply)\n- `delete.go` \u2014 handles DELETE\n- `watch.go` \u2014 handles long-running WATCH requests\n\n**`filters/`** contains the per-request HTTP middleware (authentication, authorization, audit, timeout, panic recovery, etc.) that are assembled into the handler chain.\n\n**`request/`** provides context helpers for storing and retrieving per-request information (user info, namespace, request info) from `context.Context`.\n\n### 2.3 `pkg/admission/` \u2014 Admission Control\n\nThe admission framework is defined in `interfaces.go`:\n\n```go\ntype MutationInterface interface {\n    Interface\n    Admit(ctx context.Context, a Attributes, o ObjectInterfaces) (err error)\n}\n\ntype ValidationInterface interface {\n    Interface\n    Validate(ctx context.Context, a Attributes, o ObjectInterfaces) (err error)\n}\n```\n\n`Attributes` (line 31) provides the admission plugin with everything it needs: the object being mutated, the old object (for updates), the user info, the operation type, and whether it is a dry run. The `IsDryRun()` method (line 52) is critical: plugins with external side effects must check this flag to avoid acting on dry-run requests.\n\n`chain.go` implements `chainAdmissionHandler`, a slice of `Interface` values. `Admit` iterates the chain and calls each mutator in order, returning immediately on the first error. `Validate` does the same for validators. This means **mutation always runs before validation** \u2014 the two passes are separate.\n\n`plugins/` contains built-in plugins:\n- `webhook/` \u2014 MutatingAdmissionWebhook and ValidatingAdmissionWebhook\n- `cel/` \u2014 ValidatingAdmissionPolicy (CEL-based policy engine)\n- `namespace/` \u2014 NamespaceLifecycle (prevents operations in terminating namespaces)\n- `resourcequota/` \u2014 ResourceQuota enforcement\n- `policy/` \u2014 PodSecurity admission\n\n### 2.4 `pkg/registry/` \u2014 REST Storage Abstractions\n\n**`registry/rest/rest.go`** defines the storage interface hierarchy. The key interfaces are:\n- `rest.Storage` \u2014 base interface with `Destroy()`\n- `rest.Getter` \u2014 `Get(ctx, name, options)`\n- `rest.Lister` \u2014 `List(ctx, options)`\n- `rest.Creater` \u2014 `Create(ctx, name, obj, createValidation, options)`\n- `rest.Updater` \u2014 `Update(ctx, name, objInfo, createValidation, updateValidation, forceAllowCreate, options)`\n- `rest.GracefulDeleter` \u2014 `Delete(ctx, name, deleteValidation, options)`\n- `rest.Watcher` \u2014 `Watch(ctx, options)`\n- `rest.StandardStorage` \u2014 aggregates all of the above\n\n**`registry/generic/registry/store.go`** provides `Store`, the generic implementation of `StandardStorage`. It is designed to be embedded in resource-specific storage types. Its key fields are:\n\n```go\ntype Store struct {\n    NewFunc         func() runtime.Object\n    NewListFunc     func() runtime.Object\n    KeyRootFunc     func(ctx context.Context) string\n    KeyFunc         func(ctx context.Context, name string) (string, error)\n    CreateStrategy  rest.RESTCreateStrategy\n    UpdateStrategy  rest.RESTUpdateStrategy\n    DeleteStrategy  rest.RESTDeleteStrategy\n    Storage         DryRunnableStorage\n    // ... hooks: BeginCreate, AfterCreate, BeginUpdate, AfterUpdate, AfterDelete\n}\n```\n\nThe `Strategy` objects (`RESTCreateStrategy`, `RESTUpdateStrategy`, `RESTDeleteStrategy`) are where resource-specific business logic lives: field defaulting, validation, name generation, and immutability enforcement. The `Store` calls into these strategies at the appropriate points in each CRUD operation.\n\n**`registry/generic/storage_decorator.go`** defines `StorageDecorator`, a function type that wraps a raw `storage.Interface` (typically the etcd3 client) with the watch cache. The default decorator used in production is `generic.UndecoratedStorage` for the event resource and the cacher-wrapped version for everything else.\n\n### 2.5 `pkg/storage/` \u2014 Storage Layer\n\n**`storage/interfaces.go`** defines `storage.Interface`, the abstract key-value store contract:\n- `Create`, `Delete`, `Watch`, `WatchList`, `Get`, `GetList`, `GuaranteedUpdate`\n- `Versioner` \u2014 maps between etcd `mod_revision` and Kubernetes `resourceVersion`\n\n**`storage/etcd3/`** \u2014 the concrete etcd3 implementation of `storage.Interface`.\n\n**`storage/cacher/cacher.go`** \u2014 the in-memory watch cache. It wraps a `storage.Interface` and maintains a `watchCache` (a ring buffer of recent events) plus a `store` (a snapshot of all current objects). The cacher serves most `List` and `Watch` requests from memory, falling back to etcd only when the cache's event buffer is insufficient.\n\n**`storage/value/`** \u2014 the encryption transformer layer. `ResourceTransformers` in `Config` plugs in here, enabling at-rest encryption of etcd values.\n\n### 2.6 `pkg/server/options/` \u2014 Configuration Composition\n\n`RecommendedOptions` (`options/recommended.go`) is the standard entry point for building an extension API server. It bundles:\n\n```go\ntype RecommendedOptions struct {\n    Etcd           *EtcdOptions\n    SecureServing  *SecureServingOptionsWithLoopback\n    Authentication *DelegatingAuthenticationOptions\n    Authorization  *DelegatingAuthorizationOptions\n    Audit          *AuditOptions\n    Features       *FeatureOptions\n    CoreAPI        *CoreAPIOptions\n    Admission      *AdmissionOptions\n    EgressSelector *EgressSelectorOptions\n    Traces         *TracingOptions\n}\n```\n\n`ApplyTo(config *server.RecommendedConfig)` applies each option group to the config in dependency order (etcd \u2192 egress \u2192 TLS \u2192 auth \u2192 audit \u2192 features \u2192 admission). This is the canonical way to configure an aggregated API server.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Request Flow\n\n### 3.1 Server Chain Routing\n\nWhen `kube-apiserver` receives a request, it first enters the **Aggregator Server** (built by `kube-aggregator`). The aggregator checks whether an `APIService` object has claimed the request's group/version path. If so, it proxies the request to the backing extension API server. If not, it delegates to the **Kube API Server** (core), which handles built-in groups (`core/v1`, `apps/v1`, etc.). If the core server cannot handle the path, it delegates to the **API Extensions Server** (`apiextensions-apiserver`), which handles CRD-backed resources. If none of the three servers match, the `emptyDelegate` at the end of the chain returns a 404.\n\nThe delegation mechanism is implemented via `DelegationTarget.UnprotectedHandler()`. In `completedConfig.New()` (line 803 of `config.go`):\n\n```go\napiServerHandler := NewAPIServerHandler(name, c.Serializer, handlerChainBuilder,\n    delegationTarget.UnprotectedHandler())\n```\n\nThe `delegationTarget.UnprotectedHandler()` becomes the `notFoundHandler` of the current server's `NonGoRestfulMux`. When no route matches, the mux calls this handler, which is the next server in the chain.\n\n### 3.2 Handler Chain (Filter Pipeline)\n\nEvery request that enters a `GenericAPIServer` passes through `FullHandlerChain`, which is built by `BuildHandlerChainFunc` (defaulting to `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` in `config.go`). The filters are applied in reverse order of wrapping (outermost first):\n\n1. **Panic recovery** \u2014 catches panics and returns 500\n2. **Request timeout** \u2014 enforces `RequestTimeout` for non-long-running requests\n3. **CORS** \u2014 adds CORS headers if configured\n4. **HSTS** \u2014 adds HSTS headers\n5. **Audit** \u2014 begins audit event recording for the request\n6. **Authentication** \u2014 calls the union authenticator; populates `user.Info` in context. The body is **not yet read**.\n7. **Impersonation** \u2014 checks and applies impersonation headers\n8. **Authorization** \u2014 calls the union authorizer with the user info and request attributes. Still no body deserialization.\n9. **Priority and Fairness** \u2014 classifies the request into a `FlowSchema` and `PriorityLevel`, queues or rejects based on concurrency limits\n10. **Wait group tracking** \u2014 registers the request with `NonLongRunningRequestWaitGroup` or `WatchRequestWaitGroup` for graceful shutdown\n11. **Director** \u2192 `GoRestfulContainer` or `NonGoRestfulMux`\n\n### 3.3 REST Handler Dispatch (CREATE example)\n\nOnce the filter chain passes the request to the go-restful container, the `APIInstaller`-registered handler for the resource and verb is invoked. For a `POST /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/default/deployments`, the `createHandler` function in `pkg/endpoints/handlers/create.go` executes:\n\n1. **Extract namespace/name** from URL via `scope.Namer.Name(req)` (line 61)\n2. **Negotiate output media type** \u2014 determines response format (JSON, YAML, Protobuf)\n3. **Read body** \u2014 `limitedReadBodyWithRecordMetric` enforces `MaxRequestBodyBytes` (line 94). This is the **first point** where the request body is consumed.\n4. **Decode** \u2014 `decoder.Decode(body, &defaultGVK, original)` converts the wire bytes to the internal hub version via the `Scheme`'s conversion functions (line 127)\n5. **Field validation** \u2014 if `fieldValidation=Strict`, uses a strict decoder that rejects unknown fields\n6. **Wipe system fields** \u2014 `rest.WipeObjectMetaSystemFields` clears server-managed fields like `resourceVersion`, `uid`, `creationTimestamp` from the incoming object (line 171)\n7. **Field manager update** \u2014 `scope.FieldManager.UpdateNoErrors` applies server-side apply field ownership tracking (line 199)\n8. **Admission** \u2014 `finisher.FinishRequest` calls the admission chain:\n   - First `Admit` (mutation pass) \u2014 all `MutationInterface` plugins run in order\n   - Then `Validate` (validation pass) \u2014 all `ValidationInterface` plugins run in order\n   - The `CreateStrategy.Validate` is called inside `r.Create()` as `createValidation`\n9. **Store** \u2014 `r.Create(ctx, name, obj, createValidation, options)` calls `Store.Create`, which:\n   - Calls `CreateStrategy.PrepareForCreate` (sets defaults, clears status)\n   - Calls `CreateStrategy.Validate` (business logic validation)\n   - Calls `storage.Interface.Create` \u2192 etcd3 client \u2192 etcd\n10. **Serialize response** \u2014 the stored object is converted back to the requested version and serialized\n\n### 3.4 Watch Cache Flow\n\nFor `GET /apis/apps/v1/deployments?watch=true`, the request reaches `Store.Watch`, which calls `storage.Interface.Watch`. In production, this `storage.Interface` is the `Cacher` (from `storage/cacher/cacher.go`), not the raw etcd client.\n\nThe `Cacher` maintains:\n- A `watchCache` ring buffer (default ~75 seconds of events, controlled by `DefaultEventFreshDuration = defaultBookmarkFrequency + 15s`)\n- A `store` snapshot of all current objects (populated via an initial LIST from etcd)\n- A background goroutine that watches etcd and feeds events into the ring buffer\n\nWhen a watch request arrives, the cacher creates a `cacheWatcher` and registers it. The cacher dispatches events from its ring buffer to all registered watchers. If a watcher's requested `resourceVersion` is older than the ring buffer's oldest event, the cacher falls back to a direct etcd watch for that watcher.\n\nFor consistent reads (LIST with `resourceVersion=`), the cacher fetches the latest `mod_revision` from etcd, waits until its internal cache has caught up to that revision, then serves the list from memory \u2014 avoiding a full etcd scan.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 Concurrency Limits\n\n`Config` exposes two hard concurrency limits:\n- `MaxRequestsInFlight` \u2014 maximum parallel non-mutating requests (default 400)\n- `MaxMutatingRequestsInFlight` \u2014 maximum parallel mutating requests (default 200)\n\nThese are enforced by the `WithMaxInFlightLimit` filter in the handler chain. When the limit is reached, new requests receive a `429 Too Many Requests` with a `Retry-After` header. These limits are a blunt instrument; the **Priority and Fairness** (APF) subsystem (`pkg/util/flowcontrol/`) provides finer-grained control via `FlowSchema` and `PriorityLevelConfiguration` objects, classifying requests by user, verb, and resource into queues with configurable concurrency shares.\n\n### 4.2 Watch Cache Tradeoffs\n\nThe watch cache dramatically reduces etcd read load \u2014 in a large cluster, thousands of controllers each watching thousands of objects would overwhelm etcd without it. However:\n\n- **Memory pressure**: The cache holds all objects of each resource type in memory. A cluster with millions of events or very large objects can exhaust apiserver memory.\n- **Stale reads**: By default, LIST requests are served from cache. A client that needs a guaranteed-fresh read must use `resourceVersion=0` (served from cache) or `resourceVersion=\"\"` (consistent read, which still uses the cache but waits for it to catch up to the latest etcd revision).\n- **Ring buffer overflow**: If the cacher's event ring buffer fills up (because a watcher is too slow), the watcher is forcibly closed and must re-list. This is logged as a \"watch buffer full\" event.\n- **Bookmark events**: The cacher sends periodic bookmark events (every `defaultBookmarkFrequency = 1 minute`) to advance watchers' `resourceVersion` even when no objects change, preventing expensive re-lists.\n\n### 4.3 Optimistic Concurrency\n\nThe `resourceVersion` field on every Kubernetes object maps directly to etcd's `mod_revision`. When a client submits a PUT or PATCH, the apiserver passes the client's `resourceVersion` as a precondition to `storage.Interface.GuaranteedUpdate`. If the etcd `mod_revision` has advanced (another writer modified the object), etcd rejects the write and the apiserver returns `409 Conflict` with the message defined in `store.go`:\n\n```go\nconst OptimisticLockErrorMsg = \"the object has been modified; please apply your changes to the latest version and try again\"\n```\n\nThis forces clients into a read-modify-write loop. Server-Side Apply (`managedFields`) is an alternative that avoids this by tracking field ownership, allowing multiple managers to update disjoint fields without conflicts.\n\n### 4.4 Admission Plugin Ordering and Re-invocation\n\nMutation plugins run before validation plugins. Within each pass, plugins run in the order they are registered. If a mutating webhook modifies an object, other mutating webhooks that have already run may need to re-run to account for the change. The `ReinvocationContext` interface (in `admission/interfaces.go`) and `reinvocation.go` implement this re-invocation policy: a plugin can call `SetShouldReinvoke()` to signal that the chain should be re-run.\n\nThis creates a potential for infinite loops if two plugins keep triggering each other's re-invocation. The framework limits re-invocation to a single additional pass.\n\n### 4.5 Graceful Shutdown Complexity\n\nThe shutdown sequence in `RunWithContext` (`genericapiserver.go`, lines 525\u2013700+) is deliberately multi-phase to avoid dropping in-flight requests when a load balancer is still routing traffic to the server:\n\n```\nT0:       SIGTERM received \u2192 ShutdownInitiated \u2192 /readyz returns failure\nT0+70s:   AfterShutdownDelayDuration \u2192 PreShutdownHooks run\n          \u2192 NotAcceptingNewRequest\n          \u2192 NonLongRunningRequestWaitGroup.Wait() (up to 60s)\n          \u2192 WatchRequestWaitGroup.Wait() (if ShutdownWatchTerminationGracePeriod > 0)\n          \u2192 InFlightRequestsDrained\n          \u2192 HTTP server stops listening\n          \u2192 AuditBackend.Shutdown()\n```\n\nThe 70-second `ShutdownDelayDuration` default gives load balancers time to detect the failing `/readyz` and stop routing new traffic. Operators running in environments with faster load balancer convergence can reduce this value.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points, Customization Hooks, and Associated Risks\n\n### 5.1 Custom Handler Chain (`BuildHandlerChainFunc`)\n\n`Config.BuildHandlerChainFunc` (line 186 of `config.go`) is a function field:\n\n```go\nBuildHandlerChainFunc func(apiHandler http.Handler, c *Config) (secure http.Handler)\n```\n\nReplacing this function allows complete control over the filter pipeline. The default is `DefaultBuildHandlerChain`. Extension API servers built with `RecommendedOptions` typically use the default.\n\n**Risk**: Replacing the handler chain incorrectly can bypass authentication or authorization. Any custom chain must call the inner `apiHandler` and must not skip the authentication/authorization filters unless the server is intentionally unauthenticated (e.g., a metrics-only endpoint).\n\n### 5.2 Admission Plugins\n\nNew admission plugins implement `MutationInterface` and/or `ValidationInterface` from `pkg/admission/interfaces.go`. They are registered via `admission.RegisterPlugin` and initialized via `PluginInitializer.Initialize`. The `RecommendedOptions.Admission.ApplyTo` call wires them into the chain.\n\n**Risk**: Mutating admission plugins that modify objects must be idempotent (re-invocation policy) and must handle `IsDryRun()` correctly. A plugin that makes external API calls on every admission request can become a latency bottleneck for the entire cluster. Webhook-based plugins add network round-trips and can cause cascading failures if the webhook endpoint is unavailable (mitigated by `failurePolicy: Ignore`).\n\n### 5.3 PostStartHooks and PreShutdownHooks\n\n`Config.AddPostStartHook(name string, hook PostStartHookFunc)` registers a function to run after the server starts listening. The hook receives a `PostStartHookContext` with a `LoopbackClientConfig` for privileged in-process API access and a `context.Context` that is cancelled when the server stops.\n\n```go\ntype PostStartHookFunc func(context PostStartHookContext) error\n```\n\nEach hook is automatically wired to a `/readyz` health check. If the hook has not completed, `/readyz` returns failure. If the hook returns a non-nil error, `klog.Fatalf` is called \u2014 the server crashes.\n\n**Risk**: A hook that blocks indefinitely will prevent the server from ever becoming ready. A hook that panics will crash the server. Hooks should be designed as mini-controllers that handle partial completion and restarts gracefully (the comment in `hooks.go` explicitly calls this out).\n\n### 5.4 Custom REST Storage (`rest.Storage` Interfaces)\n\nTo add a new resource, implement the appropriate `rest` interfaces from `pkg/registry/rest/rest.go` and register them via `APIGroupInfo.VersionedResourcesStorageMap`. The `genericregistry.Store` can be embedded to get standard CRUD behavior, with customization via `Strategy` objects.\n\n**Risk**: Implementing `rest.Updater` without implementing `rest.Creater` (or vice versa) can lead to unexpected behavior when the `APIInstaller` introspects the storage. The `Store` type assertion checks (`var _ rest.StandardStorage = &Store{}`) in `store.go` (line 252) serve as compile-time guards for the built-in implementation but not for custom implementations.\n\n### 5.5 New API Groups (`InstallAPIGroup`)\n\n`GenericAPIServer.InstallAPIGroup(apiGroupInfo *APIGroupInfo)` registers a new API group. The `APIGroupInfo` struct bundles the `Scheme`, `NegotiatedSerializer`, `ParameterCodec`, and `VersionedResourcesStorageMap`. The `APIInstaller` then registers HTTP routes for each resource.\n\n**Risk**: Registering two API groups with overlapping paths causes a panic in the go-restful container. The `PrioritizedVersions` field in `APIGroupInfo` controls which version is served at the group-level discovery endpoint; getting this wrong can cause clients to use a deprecated version.\n\n### 5.6 Storage Encryption (`ResourceTransformers`)\n\n`Config.ResourceTransformers` (line 222) plugs in at-rest encryption. The `storage/value/` package defines the `Transformer` interface. The `encryptionconfig/` package in `server/options/` provides the standard KMS-based implementation.\n\n**Risk**: Changing the encryption key or provider without a proper migration procedure will make existing etcd data unreadable. The `StorageVersionManager` tracks which storage version each resource is persisted in, enabling migration.\n\n### 5.7 Feature Gates\n\n`Config.FeatureGate` (line 169) controls which features are active. Feature gates are checked at runtime via `utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(feature)`. The `EffectiveVersion` field (line 157) enables version emulation \u2014 running a newer binary but behaving like an older version for API availability.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Operational Implications\n\n### 6.1 Performance\n\n**Watch cache sizing**: The watch cache ring buffer size is determined by `DefaultEventFreshDuration` (approximately 75 seconds of events). In clusters with high write rates, this buffer can fill quickly, causing watchers to be evicted and forced to re-list. Monitor the `apiserver_watch_cache_events_dispatched_total` and `apiserver_watch_events_dropped_total` metrics.\n\n**Admission webhook latency**: Each mutating or validating webhook adds a synchronous network round-trip to every write request. A webhook with p99 latency of 100ms will add 100ms to every `kubectl apply`. Use `timeoutSeconds` in `WebhookConfiguration` to bound this, and set `failurePolicy: Ignore` for non-critical webhooks.\n\n**Priority and Fairness**: APF (`pkg/util/flowcontrol/`) replaces the blunt `MaxRequestsInFlight` limits with per-flow queuing. Misconfigured `FlowSchema` objects can starve critical system components (e.g., the node lifecycle controller) if they are placed in a low-priority level. Monitor `apiserver_flowcontrol_rejected_requests_total` and `apiserver_flowcontrol_request_wait_duration_seconds`.\n\n**Serialization cost**: The apiserver serializes every response. For large LIST responses (e.g., listing all pods in a large cluster), this can be CPU-intensive. The `Protobuf` content type is significantly faster than JSON for large responses; `kubectl` uses JSON by default but internal components use Protobuf.\n\n### 6.2 Reliability\n\n**etcd dependency**: The apiserver is completely dependent on etcd for writes and consistent reads. An etcd partition or leader election will cause write failures. The watch cache provides read availability during brief etcd disruptions (existing watchers continue to receive events from the cache), but new consistent reads will fail.\n\n**Graceful shutdown**: The multi-phase shutdown sequence (Section 4.5) is designed to avoid dropping requests during rolling updates. Operators must ensure `ShutdownDelayDuration` is longer than the load balancer's health check interval. If the load balancer removes the server from rotation before `ShutdownDelayDuration` elapses, the delay is wasted; if it is too short, requests will be dropped.\n\n**PostStartHook failures**: A failing `PostStartHook` calls `klog.Fatalf`, crashing the server. This is intentional \u2014 a hook that cannot complete its initialization (e.g., cannot connect to etcd to install CRDs) should not allow the server to serve traffic in a partially-initialized state. However, it means a bug in a hook can prevent the server from ever starting.\n\n### 6.3 Maintainability\n\n**Code generation dependency**: The apiserver framework relies heavily on generated code (`deepcopy-gen`, `conversion-gen`, `defaulter-gen`, `openapi-gen`). Adding a new field to an API type requires re-running the generators. Forgetting to regenerate will cause runtime panics (missing `DeepCopy` methods) or incorrect behavior (missing conversion functions).\n\n**Strategy pattern**: The separation of generic CRUD logic (`Store`) from resource-specific logic (`Strategy`) is the primary maintainability mechanism. New resources should implement their business logic in a `Strategy` object and embed `Store`, rather than reimplementing CRUD from scratch. This ensures consistent behavior for features like dry-run, server-side apply, and optimistic concurrency.\n\n**Delegation chain complexity**: The three-server delegation chain makes it difficult to trace which server handles a given request path. The `muxAndDiscoveryCompleteSignals` mechanism (line 277 of `genericapiserver.go`) exists specifically to prevent 404 responses during startup when routes are still being registered across the chain.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Each server in the chain holds a reference to the next via `delegationTarget DelegationTarget` (line 220). When a request arrives for a path that the current server does not handle, it falls through to `delegationTarget.UnprotectedHandler()`.\n    78\t\n    79\t**`handler.go`** defines `APIServerHandler`, the HTTP routing core:\n    80\t\n    81\t```go\n    82\ttype APIServerHandler struct {\n    83\t    FullHandlerChain   http.Handler        // filter chain wrapping Director\n    84\t    GoRestfulContainer *restful.Container  // go-restful for /api and /apis paths\n    85\t    NonGoRestfulMux    *mux.PathRecorderMux // fallback for health, metrics, etc.\n    86\t    Director           http.Handler        // routes between the two\n    87\t}\n    88\t```\n    89\t\n    90\tThe `Director.ServeHTTP` method (line 121) inspects the request path against registered go-restful `WebService` root paths. If a match is found, it dispatches to `GoRestfulContainer`; otherwise it falls through to `NonGoRestfulMux`. This dual-mux design exists because go-restful is needed for OpenAPI generation but is too strict for delegation fallthrough.\n    91\t\n    92\t**`hooks.go`** implements `PostStartHookFunc` and `PreShutdownHookFunc`. Each `PostStartHook` is run in its own goroutine after the server starts listening. Critically, each hook is automatically wired to a `/readyz` health check (`postStartHookHealthz`) that returns failure until the hook's `done` channel is closed (line 109). This means the server will not report ready until all post-start hooks complete.\n    93\t\n    94\t**`lifecycle_signals.go`** defines the named channel-based signals that coordinate the shutdown sequence: `ShutdownInitiated`, `AfterShutdownDelayDuration`, `NotAcceptingNewRequest`, `InFlightRequestsDrained`, `HTTPServerStoppedListening`, `PreShutdownHooksStopped`, and `MuxAndDiscoveryComplete`.\n    95\t\n    96\t### 2.2 `pkg/endpoints/` \u2014 HTTP Endpoint Installation\n    97\t\n    98\t**`installer.go`** defines `APIInstaller`, which takes an `APIGroupVersion` (containing a map of resource names to `rest.Storage` implementations) and registers HTTP routes in the `GoRestfulContainer`. For each resource, it introspects which `rest` interfaces the storage implements (e.g., `rest.Getter`, `rest.Creater`, `rest.Updater`, `rest.Watcher`) and registers the corresponding HTTP verbs. The `action` struct (line 69) captures the verb, path, and parameters for each registered route.\n    99\t\n   100\t**`handlers/`** contains the per-verb HTTP handler functions:\n   101\t- `create.go` \u2014 `createHandler`: reads body, decodes, runs field manager, calls admission, calls `r.Create()`\n   102\t- `get.go` \u2014 handles GET (single object and list)\n   103\t- `update.go` \u2014 handles PUT\n   104\t- `patch.go` \u2014 handles PATCH (JSON merge, strategic merge, server-side apply)\n   105\t- `delete.go` \u2014 handles DELETE\n   106\t- `watch.go` \u2014 handles long-running WATCH requests\n   107\t\n   108\t**`filters/`** contains the per-request HTTP middleware (authentication, authorization, audit, timeout, panic recovery, etc.) that are assembled into the handler chain.\n   109\t\n   110\t**`request/`** provides context helpers for storing and retrieving per-request information (user info, namespace, request info) from `context.Context`.\n   111\t\n   112\t### 2.3 `pkg/admission/` \u2014 Admission Control\n   113\t\n   114\tThe admission framework is defined in `interfaces.go`:\n   115\t\n   116\t```go\n   117\ttype MutationInterface interface {\n   118\t    Interface\n   119\t    Admit(ctx context.Context, a Attributes, o ObjectInterfaces) (err error)\n   120\t}\n   121\t\n   122\ttype ValidationInterface interface {\n   123\t    Interface\n   124\t    Validate(ctx context.Context, a Attributes, o ObjectInterfaces) (err error)\n   125\t}\n   126\t```\n   127\t\n   128\t`Attributes` (line 31) provides the admission plugin with everything it needs: the object being mutated, the old object (for updates), the user info, the operation type, and whether it is a dry run. The `IsDryRun()` method (line 52) is critical: plugins with external side effects must check this flag to avoid acting on dry-run requests.\n   129\t\n   130\t`chain.go` implements `chainAdmissionHandler`, a slice of `Interface` values. `Admit` iterates the chain and calls each mutator in order, returning immediately on the first error. `Validate` does the same for validators. This means **mutation always runs before validation** \u2014 the two passes are separate.\n   131\t\n   132\t`plugins/` contains built-in plugins:\n   133\t- `webhook/` \u2014 MutatingAdmissionWebhook and ValidatingAdmissionWebhook\n   134\t- `cel/` \u2014 ValidatingAdmissionPolicy (CEL-based policy engine)\n   135\t- `namespace/` \u2014 NamespaceLifecycle (prevents operations in terminating namespaces)\n   136\t- `resourcequota/` \u2014 ResourceQuota enforcement\n   137\t- `policy/` \u2014 PodSecurity admission\n   138\t\n   139\t### 2.4 `pkg/registry/` \u2014 REST Storage Abstractions\n   140\t\n   141\t**`registry/rest/rest.go`** defines the storage interface hierarchy. The key interfaces are:\n   142\t- `rest.Storage` \u2014 base interface with `Destroy()`\n   143\t- `rest.Getter` \u2014 `Get(ctx, name, options)`\n   144\t- `rest.Lister` \u2014 `List(ctx, options)`\n   145\t- `rest.Creater` \u2014 `Create(ctx, name, obj, createValidation, options)`\n   146\t- `rest.Updater` \u2014 `Update(ctx, name, objInfo, createValidation, updateValidation, forceAllowCreate, options)`\n   147\t- `rest.GracefulDeleter` \u2014 `Delete(ctx, name, deleteValidation, options)`\n   148\t- `rest.Watcher` \u2014 `Watch(ctx, options)`\n   149\t- `rest.StandardStorage` \u2014 aggregates all of the above\n   150\t\n   151\t**`registry/generic/registry/store.go`** provides `Store`, the generic implementation of `StandardStorage`. It is designed to be embedded in resource-specific storage types. Its key fields are:\n   152\t\n   153\t```go\n   154\ttype Store struct {\n   155\t    NewFunc         func() runtime.Object\n   156\t    NewListFunc     func() runtime.Object\n   157\t    KeyRootFunc     func(ctx context.Context) string\n   158\t    KeyFunc         func(ctx context.Context, name string) (string, error)\n   159\t    CreateStrategy  rest.RESTCreateStrategy\n   160\t    UpdateStrategy  rest.RESTUpdateStrategy\n   161\t    DeleteStrategy  rest.RESTDeleteStrategy\n   162\t    Storage         DryRunnableStorage\n   163\t    // ... hooks: BeginCreate, AfterCreate, BeginUpdate, AfterUpdate, AfterDelete\n   164\t}\n   165\t```\n   166\t\n   167\tThe `Strategy` objects (`RESTCreateStrategy`, `RESTUpdateStrategy`, `RESTDeleteStrategy`) are where resource-specific business logic lives: field defaulting, validation, name generation, and immutability enforcement. The `Store` calls into these strategies at the appropriate points in each CRUD operation.\n   168\t\n   169\t**`registry/generic/storage_decorator.go`** defines `StorageDecorator`, a function type that wraps a raw `storage.Interface` (typically the etcd3 client) with the watch cache. The default decorator used in production is `generic.UndecoratedStorage` for the event resource and the cacher-wrapped version for everything else.\n   170\t\n   171\t### 2.5 `pkg/storage/` \u2014 Storage Layer\n   172\t\n   173\t**`storage/interfaces.go`** defines `storage.Interface`, the abstract key-value store contract:\n   174\t- `Create`, `Delete`, `Watch`, `WatchList`, `Get`, `GetList`, `GuaranteedUpdate`\n   175\t- `Versioner` \u2014 maps between etcd `mod_revision` and Kubernetes `resourceVersion`\n   176\t\n   177\t**`storage/etcd3/`** \u2014 the concrete etcd3 implementation of `storage.Interface`.\n   178\t\n   179\t**`storage/cacher/cacher.go`** \u2014 the in-memory watch cache. It wraps a `storage.Interface` and maintains a `watchCache` (a ring buffer of recent events) plus a `store` (a snapshot of all current objects). The cacher serves most `List` and `Watch` requests from memory, falling back to etcd only when the cache's event buffer is insufficient.\n   180\t\n   181\t**`storage/value/`** \u2014 the encryption transformer layer. `ResourceTransformers` in `Config` plugs in here, enabling at-rest encryption of etcd values.\n   182\t\n   183\t### 2.6 `pkg/server/options/` \u2014 Configuration Composition\n   184\t\n   185\t`RecommendedOptions` (`options/recommended.go`) is the standard entry point for building an extension API server. It bundles:\n   186\t\n   187\t```go\n   188\ttype RecommendedOptions struct {\n   189\t    Etcd           *EtcdOptions\n   190\t    SecureServing  *SecureServingOptionsWithLoopback\n   191\t    Authentication *DelegatingAuthenticationOptions\n   192\t    Authorization  *DelegatingAuthorizationOptions\n   193\t    Audit          *AuditOptions\n   194\t    Features       *FeatureOptions\n   195\t    CoreAPI        *CoreAPIOptions\n   196\t    Admission      *AdmissionOptions\n   197\t    EgressSelector *EgressSelectorOptions\n   198\t    Traces         *TracingOptions\n   199\t}\n   200\t```\n   201\t\n   202\t`ApplyTo(config *server.RecommendedConfig)` applies each option group to the config in dependency order (etcd \u2192 egress \u2192 TLS \u2192 auth \u2192 audit \u2192 features \u2192 admission). This is the canonical way to configure an aggregated API server.\n   203\t\n   204\t---\n   205\t\n   206\t## 3. End-to-End Request Flow\n   207\t\n   208\t### 3.1 Server Chain Routing\n   209\t\n   210\tWhen `kube-apiserver` receives a request, it first enters the **Aggregator Server** (built by `kube-aggregator`). The aggregator checks whether an `APIService` object has claimed the request's group/version path. If so, it proxies the request to the backing extension API server. If not, it delegates to the **Kube API Server** (core), which handles built-in groups (`core/v1`, `apps/v1`, etc.). If the core server cannot handle the path, it delegates to the **API Extensions Server** (`apiextensions-apiserver`), which handles CRD-backed resources. If none of the three servers match, the `emptyDelegate` at the end of the chain returns a 404.\n   211\t\n   212\tThe delegation mechanism is implemented via `DelegationTarget.UnprotectedHandler()`. In `completedConfig.New()` (line 803 of `config.go`):\n   213\t\n   214\t```go\n   215\tapiServerHandler := NewAPIServerHandler(name, c.Serializer, handlerChainBuilder,\n   216\t    delegationTarget.UnprotectedHandler())\n   217\t```\n   218\t\n   219\tThe `delegationTarget.UnprotectedHandler()` becomes the `notFoundHandler` of the current server's `NonGoRestfulMux`. When no route matches, the mux calls this handler, which is the next server in the chain.\n   220\t\n   221\t### 3.2 Handler Chain (Filter Pipeline)\n   222\t\n   223\tEvery request that enters a `GenericAPIServer` passes through `FullHandlerChain`, which is built by `BuildHandlerChainFunc` (defaulting to `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` in `config.go`). The filters are applied in reverse order of wrapping (outermost first):\n   224\t\n   225\t1. **Panic recovery** \u2014 catches panics and returns 500\n   226\t2. **Request timeout** \u2014 enforces `RequestTimeout` for non-long-running requests\n   227\t3. **CORS** \u2014 adds CORS headers if configured\n   228\t4. **HSTS** \u2014 adds HSTS headers\n   229\t5. **Audit** \u2014 begins audit event recording for the request\n   230\t6. **Authentication** \u2014 calls the union authenticator; populates `user.Info` in context. The body is **not yet read**.\n   231\t7. **Impersonation** \u2014 checks and applies impersonation headers\n   232\t8. **Authorization** \u2014 calls the union authorizer with the user info and request attributes. Still no body deserialization.\n   233\t9. **Priority and Fairness** \u2014 classifies the request into a `FlowSchema` and `PriorityLevel`, queues or rejects based on concurrency limits\n   234\t10. **Wait group tracking** \u2014 registers the request with `NonLongRunningRequestWaitGroup` or `WatchRequestWaitGroup` for graceful shutdown\n   235\t11. **Director** \u2192 `GoRestfulContainer` or `NonGoRestfulMux`\n   236\t\n   237\t### 3.3 REST Handler Dispatch (CREATE example)\n   238\t\n   239\tOnce the filter chain passes the request to the go-restful container, the `APIInstaller`-registered handler for the resource and verb is invoked. "**Serialization cost**: The apiserver serializes every response. For large LIST responses (e.g., listing all pods in a large cluster), this can be CPU-intensive. The `Protobuf` content type is significantly faster than JSON for large responses; `kubectl` uses JSON by default but internal components use Protobuf.\n\n### 6.2 Reliability\n\n**etcd dependency**: The apiserver is completely dependent on etcd for writes and consistent reads. An etcd partition or leader election will cause write failures. The watch cache provides read availability during brief etcd disruptions (existing watchers continue to receive events from the cache), but new consistent reads will fail.\n\n**Graceful shutdown**: The multi-phase shutdown sequence (Section 4.5) is designed to avoid dropping requests during rolling updates. Operators must ensure `ShutdownDelayDuration` is longer than the load balancer's health check interval. If the load balancer removes the server from rotation before `ShutdownDelayDuration` elapses, the delay is wasted; if it is too short, requests will be dropped.\n\n**PostStartHook failures**: A failing `PostStartHook` calls `klog.Fatalf`, crashing the server. This is intentional \u2014 a hook that cannot complete its initialization (e.g., cannot connect to etcd to install CRDs) should not allow the server to serve traffic in a partially-initialized state. However, it means a bug in a hook can prevent the server from ever starting.\n\n### 6.3 Maintainability\n\n**Code generation dependency**: The apiserver framework relies heavily on generated code (`deepcopy-gen`, `conversion-gen`, `defaulter-gen`, `openapi-gen`). Adding a new field to an API type requires re-running the generators. Forgetting to regenerate will cause runtime panics (missing `DeepCopy` methods) or incorrect behavior (missing conversion functions).\n\n**Strategy pattern**: The separation of generic CRUD logic (`Store`) from resource-specific logic (`Strategy`) is the primary maintainability mechanism. New resources should implement their business logic in a `Strategy` object and embed `Store`, rather than reimplementing CRUD from scratch. This ensures consistent behavior for features like dry-run, server-side apply, and optimistic concurrency.\n\n**Delegation chain complexity**: The three-server delegation chain makes it difficult to trace which server handles a given request path. The `muxAndDiscoveryCompleteSignals` mechanism (line 277 of `genericapiserver.go`) exists specifically to prevent 404 responses during startup when routes are still being registered across the chain.\n\n---\n\n## 7.
